**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories:

Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. **July 2025**

**Area 1: The Epstein Files Controversy**
(Importance: 10/10)

This briefing leads with the escalating national controversy surrounding the Jeffrey Epstein files, which has become the most dominant political issue of the day. The matter is creating significant internal conflict within the President’s political base, fracturing key alliances, and prompting unified, aggressive calls for transparency from the opposition. The situation is highly volatile and represents a direct challenge to the administration’s messaging control.

**Topic 1.1: Department of Justice and FBI Actions**
At the center of the controversy are new revelations from the Department of Justice. A recently surfaced DOJ memo indicates that federal investigators now believe Jeffrey Epstein victimized over 1,000 individuals over a span of two decades, a number that drastically exceeds all previous public knowledge and adds immense pressure to the case [1]. In a development reflecting the political sensitivity of the situation, FBI Director Kash Patel has been forced to publicly deny rumors that he is considering quitting his post over a related DOJ ruling on the files, moving to quash speculation of high-level dissent within federal law enforcement [2].

President Trump is actively and publicly attempting to quell the political blowup over the files within his MAGA base, expressing his displeasure by stating, "'I don’t like what’s happening'" and explicitly calling for supporters to end their "'Epstein Files' obsession" [1, 2]. He has also used his platform to defend Attorney General Pam Bondi from increasingly sharp attacks by those he refers to as his "'so-called' friends" [3]. **Area 2: Economic Policy & International Trade**
(Importance: 9/10)

The Administration is pursuing an aggressive, tariff-focused trade policy that is triggering sharp international blowback and forcing a strategic economic realignment among traditional U.S. allies and partners.

**Topic 2.1: New Tariffs and Trade Strategy**
The administration has formally announced it will impose, or is directly threatening to impose, across-the-board tariffs of 30% on goods from both Mexico and the European Union [1]. This hardline strategy has drawn immediate concern from trade policy experts, with one warning that under "Trump's law of the jungle," existing U.S. trade agreements "aren't worth the paper they're printed on" [2]. More critical commentary suggests the policy is creating international "chaos" and projects an image of weakness rather than strength [3].

Both the European Union and Mexico have issued official statements criticizing the proposed 30% tariffs [1]. Beyond diplomatic condemnation, reporting indicates that the policy is accelerating a major strategic shift among global partners. This realignment is particularly evident in Asia, where countries, feeling "under attack" by the tariffs, are intensifying their search for "better friends" and more reliable economic partnerships to hedge against U.S. unpredictability [3].

Domestic economic analyses point to potentially damaging long-term consequences of current administration policies for the U.S. economy. A primary concern, detailed in one report, is the risk of a national "brain drain." The combination of "research-funding cuts and immigration changes" threatens to erode America’s key economic advantages by compelling highly skilled individuals to leave for more stable opportunities abroad [1]. **Topic 3.1: Administration's Deportation Policies and Aims**
An internal ICE memo, now public, details a plan to deport migrants to countries where they are not citizens, signaling a significant escalation in enforcement authority and tactics [1]. While President Trump has publicly framed his policy as a mission to deport "'the worst of the worst,'" reporting from the Associated Press, which cites government data, suggests that official records tell a different and more complex story about who is being targeted [2]. Meanwhile, Secretary of Homeland Security Kristi Noem is publicly promoting recent enforcement activities, including immigration arrests in Tampa and a program she has dubbed "Alligator Alcatraz" [3].

### 1.2. President Trump's Calls for De-escalation
President Trump is actively and publicly attempting to quell the political blowup over the files within his MAGA base, expressing his displeasure by stating, "'I don’t like what’s happening'" and explicitly calling for supporters to end their "'Epstein Files' obsession" [1, 2]. He has also used his platform to defend Attorney General Pam Bondi from increasingly sharp attacks by those he refers to as his "'so-called' friends" [3]. When pressed by Fox News on whether he would release the documents, the President expressed significant caution, stating, “You don’t want to affect people’s lives if it’s phony stuff in there, because it’s a lot of phony stuff with that whole world” [4]. Critical media outlets have characterized the President’s increasingly urgent interventions as a "freaked-out" plea or a "meltdown" [5], with some commentary interpreting his reluctance as a definitive sign that he does not want the files released at all [6].

### 1.3. Internal MAGA Conflict and Backlash
Reporting indicates the Epstein issue is causing a severe and public fissure within the President’s base, with one major headline declaring that "MAGA Is Tearing Itself Apart" [1]. A primary driver of this conflict is tech figure Elon Musk. He has publicly criticized the President’s defense of Attorney General Bondi and mocked his handling of the situation, repeatedly demanding that he “‘Just release the files as promised’” [2]. In an apparent attempt to calm the infighting, FBI Director Kash Patel has moved to publicly dismiss what he calls "conspiracy theories" about a supposed feud between himself and Bondi [3]. The situation has been further intensified by a Trump biographer’s unverified claim of possessing "hours and hours" of unreleased audio of Epstein discussing Trump [4]. As a result of these dynamics, some reports suggest a portion of the President’s most ardent base is now turning on him over the issue [5].

### 1.4. Congressional Opposition Calls for Full Release
Leading Democratic members of the House are seizing the opportunity presented by the internal GOP conflict to press their advantage. They are launching a unified call for the full, unredacted release of all Epstein-related files. Representative Ro Khanna has formally demanded that the House hold a vote on the matter [1], and Representative Jamie Raskin has stated unequivocally that "'Everything should be released'" [2]. Adding a more personal and aggressive charge, Representative Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez has directly accused President Trump of withholding the files [3].

## 2. Economic Policy and International Trade

### 2.1. New Tariffs and Trade Strategy
The administration has formally announced it will impose, or is directly threatening to impose, across-the-board tariffs of 30% on goods from both Mexico and the European Union [1]. This hardline strategy has drawn immediate concern from trade policy experts, with one warning that under "Trump's law of the jungle," existing U.S. trade agreements "aren't worth the paper they're printed on" [2]. More critical commentary suggests the policy is creating international "chaos" and projects an image of weakness rather than strength [3].

[1] Trump announces tariffs of 30% on Mexico and the European Union, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/12/business/trump-tariff-mexico-european-union  
[2] Trump's law of the jungle means U.S. trade deals aren't worth the paper they're printed on, trade expert warns, https://fortune.com/2025/07/12/trump-administration-trade-deals-law-of-the-jungle-wto/  
[3] Trump’s tariff chaos is making him look weaker by the day, https://inews.co.uk/opinion/trumps-tariff-chaos-is-making-him-look-weaker-by-the-day-3803161  

### 2.2. International Responses and Strategic Realignment
Both the European Union and Mexico have issued official statements criticizing the proposed 30% tariffs [1]. Beyond diplomatic condemnation, reporting indicates that the policy is accelerating a major strategic shift among global partners. U.S. allies are now reportedly engaged in active efforts to "redraw the world’s trade map, minus the U.S." [2]. This realignment is particularly evident in Asia, where countries, feeling "under attack" by the tariffs, are intensifying their search for "better friends" and more reliable economic partnerships to hedge against U.S. unpredictability [3].

[1] The EU and Mexico criticise Donald Trump for proposed 30% tariff, https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cyvj13d9ylpo  
[2] American Allies Want to Redraw the World’s Trade Map, Minus the U.S., https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/13/world/europe/trump-tariffs-trade-europe-us.html?smid=nytcore-ios-share&referringSource=articleShare  
[3] Under Attack by Trump’s Tariffs, Asian Countries Seek Out Better Friends, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/13/business/economy/trump-tariffs-trade-deals.html?smid=re-share  

### 2.3. Domestic Economic Impacts and Analyses
Domestic economic analyses point to potentially damaging long-term consequences of current administration policies for the U.S. economy. A primary concern, detailed in one report, is the risk of a national "brain drain." The combination of "research-funding cuts and immigration changes" threatens to erode America’s key economic advantages by compelling highly skilled individuals to leave for more stable opportunities abroad [1]. Furthermore, a separate analysis concludes that the administration cannot achieve its own stated economic growth goals without significantly higher levels of legal immigration than are currently being contemplated [2].

[1] America’s Brain Drain Could Become the World’s Brain Gain | Research-funding cuts and immigration changes threaten some of America’s economic advantages, https://www.wsj.com/politics/policy/us-brain-drain-recruitment-02df18a7

## 3. Immigration Policy and Enforcement

### 3.1. Administration's Deportation Policies and Aims
An internal ICE memo, now public, details a plan to deport migrants to countries where they are not citizens, signaling a significant escalation in enforcement authority and tactics [1]. While President Trump has publicly framed his policy as a mission to deport "'the worst of the worst,'" reporting from the Associated Press, which cites government data, suggests that official records tell a different and more complex story about who is being targeted [2]. Meanwhile, Secretary of Homeland Security Kristi Noem is publicly promoting recent enforcement activities, including immigration arrests in Tampa and a program she has dubbed "Alligator Alcatraz" [3].

[1] ICE memo outlines plan to deport migrants to countries where they are not citizens, https://www.washingtonpost.com/immigration/2025/07/12/immigrants-deportations-trump-ice-memo/  
[2] Trump says he wants to deport 'the worst of the worst.' Government data tells another story, https://apnews.com/article/fact-check-trump-immigration-crime-ice-criminal-dangerous-violent-99557d9d68642004193a9f4b7668162e  
[3] Kristi Noem touts Alligator Alcatraz, immigration arrests in Tampa, https://www.tampabay.com/news/florida-politics/2025/07/12/kristi-noem-touts-alligator-alcatraz-immigration-arrests-tampa/  

### 3.2. ICE Enforcement Actions and Reported Consequences
Recent ICE actions have reportedly resulted in fatalities and other severe outcomes. In California, a farmworker died after falling from a greenhouse roof during what was described as a chaotic ICE raid; his death is being widely reported as the first to be directly linked to the new wave of federal raids [1]. In a separate raid on a California pot farm, authorities discovered 10 children in what they described as a situation of "potential human trafficking" [2]. A university professor was also reportedly taken into custody by immigration officials while participating in a protest against one of the raids [3]. This has led to highly critical commentary that characterizes the events as part of an ICE "Campaign of Violence," with one outlet warning that the actions of a "secret police force behaving with utter impunity" will inevitably lead to more deaths [4].

[1] California farmworker who fell from greenhouse roof during chaotic ICE raid dies, https://apnews.com/article/jaime-alanis-immigrant-farmworker-death-raid-c3c6f60a087f5f9f1d2b053fcef35b57?utm_source=reddit&utm_medium=share  
[2] 10 illegal migrant kids found at raided California pot farm: ‘Looks like potential human trafficking’, https://nypost.com/2025/07/11/us-news/10-illegal-migrant-kids-found-at-california-pot-farm-as-feds-launch-child-labor-probe/?utm_source=reddit.com&utm_source=reddit.com  
[3] Labor union says California university professor was taken during Camarillo immigration raid protest, https://ktla.com/news/local-news/labor-union-says-california-university-professor-was-taken-during-camarillo-immigration-raid-protest/

### 3.3. State and Local Government Responses
Local jurisdictions are beginning to implement countermeasures in direct response to the federal enforcement push. The city of Los Angeles has announced it will create a program to provide direct cash assistance to local immigrants who have been negatively affected by the recent federal raids [1].

## 4. Environmental Issues and National Disasters

### 4.1. The Texas Floods and Preparedness Debate
Texas is currently recovering from a deadly flash flood that has prompted a widespread, community-led relief effort as the death toll continues to rise [1]. National analysis of the event is framing it not as an isolated tragedy, but as a stark "preview of the chaos to come" in an era of climatic instability [2]. This is amplified by reporting which suggests that Texas, despite being the nation’s most disaster-prone state, maintains a political culture that is deeply "allergic to preparing for disasters," reflecting a political mood against preventative investment [3]. When asked in a Fox News interview for his response to the tragedy, President Trump suggested, "'Maybe they should’ve had bells'" [4].

### 4.2. Administration's Approach to Climate and Research
The administration is reportedly taking concrete steps to alter the federal government’s scientific apparatus and focus. Most notably, the State Department has fired multiple employees whose specific job functions were centered on climate change [1]. This development coincides with broader reporting that alleges the administration is actively "gutting weather science," a move that critics argue is directly "reducing disaster response" capabilities for the entire nation [2].

## 5. U.S. Domestic Politics and Legal Affairs

### 5.1. Congressional Affairs and Leadership
On Capitol Hill, Senate Minority Leader Chuck Schumer is reportedly threatening to force a government shutdown, a high-stakes legislative maneuver that could potentially provoke a "revolt" within his own Democratic ranks if it falters [1]. In a related sign of political positioning for the next election cycle, one of the Democrats' most electorally vulnerable senators, Jon Ossoff of Georgia, is noticeably intensifying his public criticism of President Trump in a state the President carried in 2024 [2].

### 5.2. Intra-Party and Base Dynamics
Internal party friction is evident on both sides of the aisle. For Democrats, Zohran Mamdani's progressive victory in the New York City mayoral primary is causing a significant rift. While his supporters hail the win as proof the party doesn't need to move to the center to win [1], the victory has alarmed others. Business leaders are reportedly scrambling to find and fund an opponent [2], and some Zionist Democrats have expressed concern that his candidacy forces them to choose between their political ideals and their identity [3]. For Republicans, MAGA leaders are sounding an alarm about a "discontented" base of support, warning that growing internal strife poses "a huge risk" and has the movement "on the brink" [4].

### 5.3. Retrospectives on 2024 Assassination Attempt
Multiple media outlets are marking the one-year anniversary of the assassination attempt against then-candidate Donald Trump in Butler, Pennsylvania. The event is being widely analyzed across the political spectrum as a pivotal "turning point" in the 2024 campaign, a moment of "blood and bravado" that fundamentally "upended an election" and shook the country [1]. Reporting suggests that reminders of the attempt, and the corresponding narrative that the President was "'Saved for a reason'," have become a recurring feature and thematic touchstone of his second term in office [2].

Several distinct legal situations are developing. In a major state-level case in Georgia, a Republican official has been publicly accused by authorities of orchestrating a complex Ponzi scheme that allegedly defrauded investors of $140 million [1]. In Florida, a state program called "Hope Florida," previously championed by state leadership, is now facing scrutiny over "odd, unexplained payments" that have raised questions about its management [2]. At the federal level, critical commentary has accused the Supreme Court of backing "'executive lawlessness,'" though the headline does not specify which case or ruling prompted the charge [3].
